Introduction

"Outline of Rayon Manufacturing Methods"

Rayon is a major invention of the 19th-century chemical industry and is now an important raw material for human clothing. Its position in international trade is increasingly important. In terms of output, the United States, Britain, and Japan are the most productive, while Italy and France are the leading exporters. China's consumption of rayon has consistently been over one million dan in recent years, several times more than silk. The outflow of money is incalculable. Therefore, establishing factories to manufacture rayon to stem the outflow is essential. However, due to the lack of both talent and capital, although this idea has been advocated, it has not yet been realized. Mr. Pan Xiaochun studied chemical engineering in Japan in his early years. Since returning to China, he has been employed at the Shanghai Textile Printing and Dyeing Factory. Based on his knowledge and experience, he recently compiled the book "Outline of Rayon Manufacturing Methods," which has been published by the factory's publishing department (Wufu Lane, Tianjin Road). (Priced at half a yuan in national currency.) The book thoroughly explores the history of rayon invention and its manufacturing methods, analyzing them in great detail. It also focuses on comparing various manufacturing methods and judging their properties to distinguish their merits and demerits. This book is unprecedented in China's publishing industry. All silk merchants and chemical researchers should have a copy to study.

Northern and Southern Cities Bean and Rice Industry

Calibration of New Standard Measures Yesterday

To Eliminate Malpractices in the Industry and Ensure Fair Business

Over 1,600 Measures Submitted by Various Businesses for Calibration

The Dagong News Agency reports that since the new system of weights and measures was actively promoted and implemented by the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs in 1931, the grain, bean, and rice industries in this city were the first to adopt it, abolishing the old "hai hu" and "sheng dou." Yesterday morning at 9:00, the Bean and Rice Industry Association held a spring calibration of the measures currently used by various businesses in the northern and southern cities at Cuixiu Hall. Details are as follows:

Supervisory Personnel: The supervisory personnel who attended yesterday included Huang Yongping from the Weights and Measures Verification Office of the Bureau of Social Affairs, Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Bean and Rice Industry Association, Standing Committee Members Zhu Zixiang and Yan Xiaoquan, Cai Yukun, Fu Qiangeng, and Chen Yuzhao representing the rice merchants in the southern city, Lu Jingwen and Qiang Zisheng from the Rice Industry Office in the northern city, and over one hundred staff members and "hu si" from various rice merchants. Chairman Gu Xinyi first reported on the calibration of the spring measures. The matter concerns the unification of the new system throughout the city, with the spirit of mutual supervision to eliminate malpractices, ensure fairness and honesty in business, and seek credibility in society.

Calibration Situation: The measures sent by various rice merchants in the northern and southern cities for calibration totaled over 1,600. During the calibration, the measures preserved by the Bean and Rice Industry Association and the Municipal "hu" of the Weights and Measures Verification Office were used as standards. The "hu si" used small black beans (due to their lack of expansibility) to calibrate each measure one by one. If the black beans overflowed (too much) or were too shallow (too little) after the measure was filled, the amount of excess or deficiency in "sheng" and "he" was estimated, and the wooden block at the bottom of the measure was removed (if too much) or added (if too little). (The wooden blocks were divided into three types: "Fu" for one "sheng," "Lu" for five "he," and "Shou" for two "he.") The method was very careful. The calibration was completed at 3:30 p.m.

Statistics on China's Exports to the US in January

The Greater America Evening News reports that, according to statistics released by the US Consul General's Office in Shanghai, the total value of goods exported from all of China, including Hong Kong, to the United States in January of this year was US$5,220,932. Non-edible animals and animal products accounted for the largest share, totaling US$2,618,626, accounting for more than 50% of the total export value for the month. Hides and skins such as lamb and goat accounted for US$870,261, and grey squirrels accounted for US$445,572. In addition, there were about 2 million pounds of raw sheepskin and lambskin, worth a total of US$444,074. The second largest category was textiles, worth US$560,439, accounting for about one-third of the total export value. The third largest category was non-edible plant products, worth US$414,321. The fourth largest category was edible animals and animal products, worth US$202,2459. The fifth largest category was plant foods and alcoholic beverages, worth US$192,094. The sixth largest category was non-metallic minerals, worth US$13,416. The value of the remaining categories was less than US$10,000.

After the Zhaoxing Steamer Abandoned Salvage Operations

Jianghai Customs Tenders for Removal

The Goods Have Been Retrieved by the Insurance Company

After the Zhaoxing Steamer Company's Zhaoxing Steamer was sunk in the Huangpu River by the Sanbei Steamer Company's Wanxiang Steamer, the Zhaoxing Company and the insurance companies that had obtained marine insurance have decided to abandon the salvage. The Jianghai Customs has tendered for the removal of the sunken ship. Details are as follows:

Abandoned Salvage

The Zhao Tai, Lian Bao, Lian Tai, Sincere, Hua An, Ning Shao, and other insurance companies that underwrote the marine insurance for the Zhaoxing Steamer, as well as the Zhaoxing Steamer Company, had telegraphed the Japanese salvage company to carry out the salvage. However, the salvage costs were too high, and salvage was actually quite difficult. Even if it were salvaged, the repair costs would be enormous. Moreover, the insurance was only 70,000 yuan, so it was not cost-effective. A decision was made today to abandon the salvage. As for the goods on board, the Union and other insurance companies that underwrote the marine insurance for the goods carried out the salvage. The goods have now been retrieved, but due to water damage, they will be auctioned off to compensate for the loss.

Customs Removal

After the Jianghai Customs Tax Office learned that the insurance companies and the Zhaoxing Steamer Company had abandoned the salvage, it issued a special announcement to tender for the removal of the sunken Zhaoxing ship. The Zhaoxing Steamer sank in the seventh section of this port and now needs to be tendered for complete removal. This tender should be submitted to the Port Director of this Customs House. The deadline for receiving the tender is noon on March 31st of this year. However, the Customs House does not limit itself to accepting the lowest or any tender price. For detailed information, please inquire at the Port Affairs Department of this Customs House. This is hereby announced. Tax Commissioner Boerlad of the Jianghai Customs, March 13, 1934, Republic of China.

Jianghai Customs

Ban on the Import of Diseased Animals and Plants

Announcement Issued Yesterday

Tang Haian, Superintendent of Jianghai Customs, and Le Zu, Tax Commissioner, issued an announcement yesterday stating that, in accordance with the government's order, the "Regulations on Banning the Import of Agricultural Pests and Diseases" shall be implemented from the date of promulgation until further notice. All live pathogens, bacteria, fungi, protozoa, and insects that harm agriculture imported from foreign countries shall be limited to the port of Shanghai for the time being. Each import must have a special permit from the Ministry of Industry and be certified by the Shanghai Inspection Bureau before being allowed to pass. These should be followed. All merchants are hereby notified. This is hereby announced.

Various Organizations Held Representative Conference Yesterday

Organized the Citizens' Legal Rights Protection Association

The Guowen News Agency reports that yesterday afternoon at 5:00, various organizations in Shanghai held a representative conference at the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. Attendees included representatives from various trade associations, municipal joint branch associations, labor unions, and hometown associations, totaling over 1,000 people. Wang Zhixiang, Liu Zhongying, and Chen Jiufeng were elected as the presidium, with Ren Xianqun as the recorder. The resolutions are as follows: (1) Establish the Shanghai Citizens' Legal Rights Protection Association; (2) Elect nine members of the preparatory committee: Zhang Xianfang, Xu Zaikang, Wei Zhiqiu, Chen Jiufeng, Liu Zhongying, Zheng Dongshan, Jin Chuxiang, Lin Jun, and Wang Zhixiang; (3) Reject the abolition of the lunar calendar for rent payment regarding the rent reduction issue; (4) Oppose secret agents representing various organizations; (5) Issue a declaration; (6) Approve the request of the Zhabei Civil Rights Protection Association to merge. The meeting adjourned at about 6:00 after a group photo was taken.

Sixteen Puli

Refrigerated Cargo Ships Robbed

The Refrigerated Cargo Association Has Asked the Police Bureau to Investigate

The Sixteen Puli Refrigerated Cargo Wharf is guarded by several patrolmen hired by the Refrigerated Fish Industry Association, who take turns patrolling to provide protection. On the evening of the 12th, while the patrolmen were on duty, they saw three small boats coming towards them in the Huangpu River. They immediately shouted to ask what was happening. Unexpectedly, more than ten people in long robes jumped out of the boats and immediately drew their hidden pistols and box cannons, aiming them at the patrolmen and shouting to stop them from making noise. They then entered various refrigerated cargo ships and carried out robberies. At the time, the patrolmen, lacking the ability to defend themselves, had no choice but to let them do what they wanted. As a result, the losses of the various ships were over a thousand yuan. The matter was reported to the Refrigerated Cargo Association, which submitted a report to the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team Leader Zhu to request that more patrolmen be dispatched to thoroughly investigate.

Emergency Relief for the Zhabei Fire Concluded

The victims of the recent Zhabei fire were mostly coolies from Jiangbei. Wen Lan Ting, Chairman of the Executive Committee of the Chinese Red Cross Society, and Wang Pei Yuan, Director-General, and others, gathered to discuss and provide relief, as previously reported. Yesterday morning, staff members Li Nai Shuang, Wu Yu Lin, Zhang Yi Kun, and Huang Shou Kang, together with Inspector Li Qing Jie and Patrol Chief Yang from the Taiyang Temple Police Station in the Fourth District, went to the secondary fire-stricken area to distribute rice coupons according to the register. However, the fire-stricken area was wider than the previous Jingjiang Road area, so more rice coupons were issued than last time, totaling over 5,000 coupons for four liters of rice each. Maintaining order was quite difficult due to the large population. Fortunately, Inspector Li and Patrol Chief Yang directed effectively, so there were no disturbances during the distribution of rice coupons. Work Relief in the Hebei Disaster Area

Can Be Fully Completed Within the Next Month

According to the Central News Agency, after Kong Xiang Rong, Director of the Work Relief Group of the Yellow River Flood Relief Committee, went to the disaster area for inspection, he felt that the disaster area lacked materials such as bricks and burlap bags for blocking water inlets. He immediately telegraphed various parties to order six batches of materials, which were shipped in batches, in order to speed up the project. According to news from the group yesterday, the work relief projects in the disaster area, except for the complete completion of the Shandong and Henan areas, have also completed most of the Hebei area. The project in this area could have been completed earlier, but was delayed due to a lack of materials. It is now learned that a considerable amount of bricks and other materials for blocking breaches in Changyuan, Shitou Zhuang, and other places has been transported to the area. It is estimated that all the required materials can be gathered by the end of this week, and construction can begin simultaneously to block the breaches, so that the project can be fully completed within the next month.

Gansu Provincial Relief Committee

Cables Thanks for Donations from the Emergency Relief Association

Requests that the Central Bank Directly Remit to Lanzhou

The Gansu Provincial Relief Committee, due to the vast disaster area in the province and the lack of relief funds, recently received donations from the joint association of charitable organizations in this city. Yesterday, they specially cabled their thanks to the association, saying: "To the Shanghai Charitable Organizations' Joint Association for Raising Emergency Relief Funds for the Yellow River Flood: We have received instructions from the Gansu Provincial Government that your association has raised 1,000 yuan in relief funds for Gansu Province. Please determine the remittance method immediately and inform us by telegraph so that the funds can be remitted to Gansu as soon as possible. We are deeply grateful upon hearing this good news. Last year's floods in Gansu Province affected as many as fifty counties. Although we have made every effort to appeal for relief funds, we have not received a single cent. As winter passed, countless disaster victims died from hunger and cold. Now, as the season for spring warming and sowing arrives, the disaster-stricken areas are requesting seeds. Our association has appealed without response, and we lack the means to provide relief. Our compatriots in the disaster area are sitting and waiting for death. Now, we have received 1,000 yuan in donations, which is truly a boundless blessing. Please transfer the funds through the Central Bank to Lanzhou. The remittance fee, whatever it may be, should be deducted from the donation. We also earnestly request that you widely publicize the disaster situation in Gansu Province. We will see that the benevolent spirit will reach countless lives. We hereby send this cable to express our sincere gratitude and thank you for your great kindness. Respectfully, the Gansu Provincial Relief Committee, note from National Customs."

Achievements in Seizing Contraband such as Opium

According to the reports of the Customs Commissioners, the quantity of contraband such as opium and morphine seized in July, August, and September of the 22nd year of the Republic of China is as follows: A total of 10,480 taels, 3 mace, and 4 fen of foreign and native opium; 379 taels, 3 mace, and 6 fen of foreign and native opium paste; 28 taels of opium powder; 47 taels of opium dross; 143 taels and 8 mace of morphine; 658 taels, 2 mace, and 5 fen of heroin and other drugs; 18 catties of poppy seeds and poppy husks; and various medicinal products containing toxic substances valued at 2,070 yuan and 1 jiao in national currency, and 21 gold units.

Dance Girl Yin Qiu Lian

Sues for Loss of Beauty

Scars on the Face Caused by Being Beaten by Gao Li Li Are Still Visible

Income Greatly Affected Due to Increased Disdain from Patrons

Yin Qiu Lian, a woman from Fengtian who used to be a dancer at the An Le Palace dance hall on Avenue Edward VII, had a disagreement with her fellow dancer Gao Li Li over a trivial matter. On the afternoon of October 23rd of last year, Yin was suddenly beaten and injured in the face. She then hired a lawyer to sue Gao Li Li for assault in the criminal court of the First Special District Court. As a result, Gao was fined 30 yuan. However, Yin Qiu Lian argued that she was a dancer who relied entirely on her beautiful face to earn income. Since being beaten by Gao,

Facial Scars

are still visible and have not yet returned to their original state, greatly affecting her income. All of these losses were caused by Gao Li Li, so she hired lawyer Jiang Zong Pan again to file a lawsuit in the civil court of the Special Court, requesting that Gao Li Li be ordered to compensate for the loss of beauty and medical expenses, totaling 3,000 yuan. Yesterday morning, Judge Yu Chang Zi presided over the hearing in the Eleventh Civil Court. The defendant, Gao Li Li, did not appear and entrusted lawyer Chao Kun to appear on her behalf. Yin Qiu Lian's statement was then presented, stating that she could not speak Chinese and wanted to

Testify in English

At this time, the defendant's representative lawyer, Chao Kun, stated that the plaintiff could actually speak very fluent Mandarin. In order to clarify the facts of the case, the judge ordered translator Mr. Pan to act as an interpreter. According to Yin, she was 22 years old, from Shenyang, and lived at 116 Bazilu. On October 5th of last year, she came to Shanghai from Qingdao. Three days later, she went to the An Le Palace dance hall on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession alone to see the manager, surnamed Jin. At that time, the defendant Gao Li Li was at the hall. Because of Gao's persuasion, she worked as a dancer at the hall. The dance fees were split equally between her and the dance hall. If she received any

Extra Tips

from patrons, she kept them all to herself. I worked as a dancer at the hall for only two weeks, earning a net income of five or ten yuan per day. Since being beaten by Gao on October 23rd of last year, I did not enter the dance hall for more than two months. Until two days before the end of last year, I worked as a dancer at the Great China Dance Hall for two days. At that time, many patrons, seeing the scars on my face, suspected that I had irregular behavior and had quarreled with guests, causing them to ridicule me, which made me feel embarrassed. Therefore, I have since

Refrained from Going

Judge Yu asked: "During the two months that you were injured, did you work as a dancer at other dance halls?" Yin replied, "No." He also asked if she had attended any large banquets. She replied, "On Christmas last year, I went to the Raffee Garden to dance once with several Chinese people." He asked, "How do you calculate the 3,000 yuan that you now want Gao Li Li to compensate you?" She replied, "Because I have not been doing business for two months, I still have to provide my own food. If the fight had not happened, I could have gone to other dance halls to work, and the income cannot be calculated. Generally, dancers mostly rely on

Beautiful Appearance

as a prerequisite, but the scars on my face are still visible. I don't know when they will recover. Although I am currently dancing at the Vienna Dance Hall, when the electric lights are on at night, my disfigured face and scars are quite obvious, causing me to be disliked by patrons and unwelcome. My livelihood is bleak, and I deeply hate it. I am currently receiving treatment from Dr. Wang, a facial specialist on Nanjing Road, who is injecting medicine. He said that it will take two months for the scars to fade. The losses I have suffered include 200 yuan in hospital and medical expenses, and 1,800 yuan in lost income of 30 yuan per day for two months. The remaining 1,000 yuan is for compensation for

Loss of Beauty

etc." After verifying the statement, the court advised them to reconcile and avoid litigation, and asked them to make concessions to each other. Yin Qiu Lian then stated that she must be compensated at least 1,000 yuan. At this time, the defendant's lawyer immediately stated that the plaintiff had previously agreed that she only needed to set up two tables and prepare two banquets of wine, each costing twelve yuan, as a reconciliation feast to resolve all previous grievances, and would not discuss anything else. Now that the court is

Kindly Reconciling

my lawyer is willing to state on behalf of the defendant that she will bear the costs of this lawsuit. At that time, because the plaintiff owed 500 yuan and was still suffering losses, she did not allow it. Now, she requests that the defendant be ordered to appear in court so that they can reconcile in person, etc. Judge Yu then ordered that the case be adjourned to attempt an out-of-court settlement. Son-in-law of He Xiang Ning

Li Mo Nong Transferred to the Garrison Headquarters

Admitted That He Is Indeed a Communist Party Member

But Still Unwilling to Confess and Repent

Li Mo Nong, the son-in-law of Central Committee member He Xiang Ning, a native of Guangdong, and Wang Wei Min, a native of Tianjin, were arrested at the intersection of Tongfu Road and Jing'an Temple Road at 9 AM on the first of this month on suspicion of being Communist Party members. They were immediately escorted by the Chengdu Road Police Department to the Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court. After three interrogations, Central Committee members Wu Zhihui, Liu Yazi, and others jointly posted bail, and they were transferred to the Public Security Bureau on the day before yesterday (the 13th). It is now learned that they have been transferred to the Garrison Headquarters. All the details are recorded below.

Three Interrogations

The first two interrogations were conducted by Judge Jiang Shu Zi on the 2nd of this month, and the third was conducted by Criminal Court President Yu Hua on the 6th of this month. For the benefit of the defendant, it was ordered that the hearing be postponed for one week to allow the defendant to present rebuttal evidence. On the morning of the day before yesterday (the 13th), the hearing was held again, still presided over by Court President Yu Hua, along with the judge and prosecutor, in the first criminal court. Legal advisors and inspectors from the Public Security Bureau were present, and lawyer Wu Kai Sheng represented the defendants. Central Committee members Wu Zhihui, Liu Yazi, Zhu Shao Ping, relatives of He Xiang Ning, and others were also present to observe the hearing.

Transferred to the Public Security Bureau

After the court session began, Court President Yu immediately inquired about the evidence from Hong Kong. Defendant's lawyer Wu Kai Sheng replied that Hong Kong was far away and the evidence favorable to the defendant could not be presented at that time. He requested another two-week postponement and permission to release the defendant on bail so that the defendant could have an opportunity for self-reflection. Subsequently, an inspector from the Public Security Bureau stated that Zhao Lin (formerly Meng Yong Xiang), who recently surrendered to the Public Security Bureau, confessed that Li Mo Nong was a Communist Party member and the current Propaganda Minister of the Jiangsu Provincial Committee, and could testify in court. Later, the police lawyer stated that the defendant had already been given the opportunity to present evidence during the second postponement, so he did not object to the transfer to the Public Security Bureau. Finally, at around 11 AM, the court transferred Li Mo Nong to the Public Security Bureau.

Wu and Liu Did Their Best

Central Committee members Wu Zhihui and Liu Yazi, along with Zhu Shao Ping and Wu Kai Sheng, immediately followed and paid a visit to Director Wen, willing to jointly guarantee his release. Yesterday, a reporter from the New Sound Society visited Peng, the Director of the Public Security Bureau, about this matter. He said that the Public Security Bureau has always handled Communist Party cases fairly according to the law. If the offender can realize his mistakes, the state is also very willing to give him a chance to reform. Therefore, Wu, Liu, and Director Wen discussed a solution at that time, which was for Li Mo Nong to first write a letter of repentance. However, Li initially denied being a Communist Party member, so Wu and others left at 7 PM.

Transferred to the Garrison Headquarters

Afterwards, the Public Security Bureau presented many relevant documents, all of which were extremely solid. After reading them, Li had to draft a confession, admitting that he was a Communist Party member. However, he still did not agree to the part about confessing and repenting. At this time, in order to make a fair judgment on legal grounds, the Public Security Bureau transferred Li Mo Nong to the Municipal Garrison Headquarters the night before last to await interrogation.

Hongchang Printing House

Forging Little Champagne Tickets

The Plot to Sell and Defraud Was Exposed

Evidence Was Thoroughly Searched and Many People Were Arrested

Recently, someone forged Little Champagne tickets for the Jiangwan draw on April 2nd of the Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Joint Association and sent people to sell them in teahouses and restaurants throughout the city. However, these forged tickets were printed quite well, making it difficult for buyers to distinguish them from the real ones, and they were easily fooled. The tickets stated that each ticket cost one yuan and that the prize for winning the first horse was 22,400 yuan. Ordinary gambling addicts all rushed to buy them, hoping to win the championship. Therefore, the sales of these forged tickets spread widely. However, the secret was leaked and detected by a detective from the First District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau. He also learned that the main printing press for these forged tickets was the Hongchang Printing House at No. 2 Heping Road, Old West Gate. He immediately reported to District Chief Guan Gong and dispatched a large number of detectives to join forces with the police chiefs of the Second District. At about 5 PM on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, they rushed to the Hongchang Printing House to conduct a search. They seized more than 2,000 forged champagne tickets on the spot. However, the manager of the house, Chang Yuan from Changzhou, and his partner had already fled upon hearing the news. Only Wu Weiming, a shareholder of the house, was guarding the door and was immediately arrested. Along with the seized evidence, he was taken back to the district. During the preliminary interrogation by District Chief Guan, Wu Weiming confessed that he was 32 years old, from Lanxi, Zhejiang Province. The forged tickets were brought in by a runner named Lu Quansheng, who entrusted him to print them. Lu currently lived at No. 29 Zhizhongli, Zilaishui Street, French Concession. He did not know anything else, etc. The detectives were then dispatched to the house along with Chinese and foreign detectives from the French Concession Police Department. Lu was out when they arrived, and his wife, Ms. XX, was at home. The detectives pretended to be partners of the Hongchang Printing House and told Lu's wife that the champagne tickets that Mr. Lu had entrusted them to print had already been printed. When Mr. Lu returned home, he could go to Hongchang to pick them up. The woman believed it to be true. When Lu returned home, his wife told him what had happened, and Lu also believed it without a doubt. When he went to the Hongchang Printing House, the police chiefs dispatched by the Second District were already secretly waiting there. As soon as Lu entered, he was immediately arrested. Liu Zhengquan from Zhenjiang, who came with Lu, was also arrested and taken back to the Second District. After District Chief Guan of the First District learned about it, he sent personnel to take them back together and conduct a preliminary interrogation. Lu confessed that he was 36 years old, from Shanghai. The forged tickets were entrusted to him for printing by Lu Jinshan from Zhenjiang, who lived upstairs at the Dongfang Shoe Store on Caishi Road, French Concession. He hesitated to say anything else. Liu's confession was evasive. Until about 11 AM yesterday morning, the detectives went to Hongchang again for a search. Unexpectedly, the model for printing the forged tickets had been taken out by Dai Rongbao, a partner of Chang Yuan's wife, so it was not found. Dai was arrested and taken to the district for interrogation. His confession was mostly evasive. Considering the importance of the case, it was ordered that they be detained separately for further investigation and arrest of accomplices, and that they be transferred to the General Bureau for strict interrogation and punishment.

Petition from Ferry Workers in Dongjiadu

Requesting to Run the Ferry Themselves

Presenting Four Reasons

Requesting to Raise Funds for Improvement

According to Da Gong She, the ferry workers in Dongjiadu, Nanshi, recently believed that if the Xingye Trust Company took over the ferry, their livelihoods would be cut off in the future, causing widespread panic. They organized a petition group the day before yesterday and petitioned the municipal government and relevant bureaus. Yesterday, they jointly submitted a petition to the municipal government, presenting four reasons and requesting to raise funds to run the ferry themselves to avoid the pain of unemployment. The original text is recorded below: "Presenting this petition because the Dongjiadu ferry is the century-old business of the common people, involving the lives of hundreds of families, men, women, old, and young. It is extremely difficult to allow the Xingye Trust Company to seize it. It should be improved by the common people raising funds to maintain their livelihoods. We respectfully present the reasons and request your kind review and approval. On the ninth of this month, the poor people received a notice from the First Section of the First District of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, stating: 'The Xingye Trust Company's letter has been approved, stating that after the company takes over the municipal ferry, it will proceed with the planning according to the established plan. It is now planned to operate the Dongjiadu ferry. The Dongjiadu situation is complex. Please inform the ferry workers to avoid misunderstandings and order them to comply without fail.' The common people were horrified upon hearing this. After returning and discussing it openly, they all agreed that there were four points that had to be clearly stated. The municipal government allowed the Xingye Trust Company to take over the ferry, and the reason it held was that the ferry operated by the common people was too old-fashioned, inconvenient for travelers, and sometimes carried too many passengers, which was dangerous. Regarding the former, during the tenure of Director Huang of the Public Works Bureau, we applied for the issuance of improved ferry regulations and ferry terminal designs to guide the improvement, but it was not approved. The responsibility for the ferry's failure to improve to this day does not lie with the common people. Regarding the latter, it only happens occasionally, and the reasons are all due to passengers who have urgent matters and need to cross the river early and ask for accommodation, and not due to the common people's intention to overload. Even if this is the fault of the common people, it can be rectified, but it cannot be used as a reason to deprive the common people of their livelihoods. As the saying goes, 'To seize the ox because it trespassed on someone else's field, the one who seized the ox is indeed guilty, but to seize the ox is not too much?' The common people occasionally carry too many passengers, and we really don't know why it is considered a crime. But to seize the century-old business and the livelihoods of hundreds of families is too much. This is the first point that must be clearly stated, that the Dongjiadu ferry should be improved by the common people and cannot be operated by the Xingye Trust Company. The principle of municipal operation is the municipal government's standard for city ferries. Whether this regulation is perfect is not up for discussion, but setting this aside, the Xingye Trust Company is a commercial organization whose business purpose is to profit and cannot be regarded as a government agency. It cannot invoke the name of the municipal government's principle of municipal operation for city ferries to seize the century-old business and the livelihoods of hundreds of families of the common people for its own operation. This is the second point that must be clearly stated, that the Dongjiadu ferry should be improved by the common people raising funds and cannot be transferred to the Xingye Trust Company. The central government has issued orders nationwide to adhere to the Three People's Principles and resist foreign economic aggression. Any violation is considered reactionary. The Principle of People's Livelihood in the Three People's Principles is of utmost importance, and the government administration should always take it into account and should not destroy it in the slightest. Foreign ships operating on the Huangpu River and inland rivers are one of the forms of economic aggression, and we should seek to run our own ships and resist them without any doubt. Since the Xingye Trust Company bears the municipal government's mission of industrial development, it should pay extreme attention to both the Principle of People's Livelihood and foreign economic aggression. However, we have not heard of any plans to compete with foreign shipping lines, but it seeks to seize the century-old business and the livelihoods of hundreds of families of the common people. Does this not contradict the central government's policy of promoting the Principle of People's Livelihood and preventing foreign economic aggression? This is the third point that must be clearly stated, that the Dongjiadu ferry should be improved by the common people raising funds and cannot be operated by the Xingye Trust Company. The Kuomintang founded the Republic of China, hoping to progress from the Three People's Principles to the Great Harmony, as shown to the nation, has been around for many years. To not claim the credit as one's own is one of the true meanings of the Great Harmony. However, in the 17th year of the Republic of China, Huang Zihe, who had no historical connection with the ferry, requested to take over the ferry, and it was allowed. Now, the Xingye Trust Company requests to take over the ferry, and it is also allowed. However, the common people, who have a century-old history and livelihoods of hundreds of families connected to the ferry, request to improve the ferry, and it has not been allowed to this day. Is it possible for Huang Zihe to achieve the merit of improving the Dongjiadu ferry, is it possible for the Xingye Trust Company to achieve it, but it is not possible for the common people who have a century-old history and livelihoods of hundreds of families connected to the Dongjiadu? There is no such principle in the Three People's Principles. This is the fourth point that must be clearly stated, that the Dongjiadu ferry should be improved by the common people raising funds and cannot be operated by the Xingye Trust Company. In summary, in addition to submitting this petition to the Public Works Bureau, we specially submit this petition to respectfully request that you allow the Xingye Trust Company to use its capital to compete with foreign shipping lines and develop its business. The Dongjiadu ferry business should be improved by the common people raising funds to maintain their livelihoods, so as to conform to the political principles of the Three People's Principles and avoid disputes. We are extremely grateful. Respectfully submitted to Wu, the Mayor of Shanghai, regarding the detention of prisoners."

Burying Feces in the Bedding

The stench was unbearable.

A prank by Xu Xiaoming and Jiang Youshou.

Deliberately destroying public property should be severely punished.

Xu A'hong from Ningbo, 45 years old, residing at 384 Zhaojia Road, worked as a tea server on the Ninghai steamer. His wife, Zhou, 42 years old, had only one son named Xiaoming, currently 20 years old. He was extremely loved as a child. When he grew up, he was recommended to learn to drive at the Lili Motor Company. Unexpectedly, Xiaoming did not pursue his studies properly and developed a rogue nature, associating only with the lowest elements. His parents repeatedly admonished him, but he did not repent and sometimes even became rebellious, causing his parents to become extremely angry and often want to expel him. However, his mother, loving her son deeply, repeatedly stopped them. A'hong considered himself as having no son and could only sigh. Recently, Xiaoming, along with the rogue Jiang Youshou, set up a gambling stall on the road, luring people to gamble. They were arrested by the Second Precinct of the First District Public Security Bureau and sentenced to a fine of five yuan each. Xu Xiaoming had no money to pay, and his father, A'hong, refused to pay, so he was sentenced to five days of detention in lieu of payment. Jiang Youshou was also sentenced to detention. Unexpectedly, Xu and Jiang not only did not abide by the rules in the detention center, but also sang operas day and night, making noise and disturbing the peace, ignoring the guards' warnings. The other prisoners were also disturbed and wanted to beat them, but were stopped by the guards. However, Xu continued to stubbornly curse and scold. Yesterday was the day Xu's detention period was completed and he was released. According to the rules of the detention center, the released prisoner's body and bedding must be checked to prevent fire hazards or contraband. The guard saw that Xu's bedding was neatly folded (the bedding was issued by the Public Security Bureau) and thought that Xu still had some redeeming qualities. Who knew that when the guard unfolded Xu's bedding, he suddenly smelled an unbearable stench. Unexpectedly, there was a large bag of excrement wrapped inside, causing the sheets to be covered in filth. This was undoubtedly Xu's deliberate prank. The guard reported to Director Liu, who questioned Xu, asking where the excrement came from. Xu Xiaoming claimed that he had an urgent need and had no choice, but it was found that the bag contained half a chamber pot's worth of excrement, which Xu and Jiang had accumulated day by day. There was no doubt that they deliberately destroyed public property. Director Liu, considering that the prisoner was so naughty and that the law could not be evaded, ordered him to be sent to the Public Security Bureau for severe punishment and then sent to the vagrant work-study center for reformation.

Jianghai Customs Notice

Attention to Ship Capacity

Issuing freight manifests must not be unrestricted

Otherwise, the right to customs refunds will not be granted

The General Affairs Section of Jianghai Customs issued a special notice yesterday stating that in the future, various shipping companies must not issue cargo manifests for export, re-export, and transit goods without restrictions. It said, "It has been found that various shipping companies often issue the aforementioned cargo manifests without restrictions, without considering the capacity of the ships. As a result, numerous goods are rejected by customs, further increasing the numerous unexpected tasks of customs officers, such as verifying goods and approving procedures. In the future, various shipping companies must pay close attention to the ship's capacity when issuing the aforementioned cargo manifests. If they are issued arbitrarily and are discovered by customs officers, they will not be allowed to enjoy the right to customs refunds. This is to be followed uniformly. This is a special notice."

Two Groups of Workers Fight

Using iron bars and wooden sticks as weapons

The ringleaders were arrested and four people were injured

Zhang Shihao from Guangdong previously worked as a craftsman at the Huasheng Electric Fan Factory. Not long after, he was recruited by the Huatong Electric Machinery Factory on Zhoujiazui Road, Aierkao Road, and transferred from Huasheng to Huatong as a foreman. However, a group of workers did not get along with Zhang and often had disputes. Recently, the workers intended to use force against Zhang, but the plan was leaked to Zhang. Therefore, Zhang Shihao also secretly plotted with a group of former workers from the Huasheng factory to deal with the situation. Yesterday afternoon at around 5:00 PM, when the two factories let out work, about 500 workers from both sides gathered near the factory gate, each thinking of starting a fight. After a disagreement, the workers from both sides immediately used iron bars and wooden sticks to beat each other, creating a loud and chaotic scene. Fortunately, the Huishan Police Station received the news and dispatched a large number of detectives to arrest them. However, when the workers saw the detectives arrive, they scattered like birds and beasts. The ringleader, Zhang Shihao, was arrested on the spot and taken to the police station for interrogation. However, Fei Xingchang, Cai Tianen, and Wang Zirong, three Huatong workers, and Zhou Shirong, a Huasheng worker, all had their heads injured by sticks and fainted on the ground. The police station dispatched a patrol car to send them to the Tongren Hospital for treatment.

Beihai Road

Red Pill Den Raided

Headquarters Located on Caishi Road

Raw Materials, Machines, Etc. Confiscated

Liu Shaokui and Song Bingzheng, Chinese detectives from the Public Concession Narcotics Department, learned that No. 8 Zhishun Lane, Beihai Road, was a red pill trafficking den. Yesterday afternoon at 3:10 PM, they led Chinese detectives Wu Hanzhang and Xie Futang, Bao detectives Zhang Changgui, etc., to search the premises. They arrested Zhang A'da, a local man, and confiscated 142 large packages of red pills, as well as silver dollars, etc. According to Zhang's confession, they learned that the headquarters was located at No. 227 Caishi Street in the French Concession, with shareholders named Ye A'hua and Chen Wanchun (also known as Huanwen). No. 227 Caishi Street was Chen's home. Detectives Liu and Song ordered two detectives to guard the house and, together with French Concession detectives, went to the address to arrest the woman Chen Ding. In a room converted from a drying platform, they confiscated a large number of red pills, as well as raw materials and machines for manufacturing red pills, totaling dozens of items. They were all taken back to the police station. The detectives guarding Beihai Road also arrested Ye A'hua and Chen Wanchun, who arrived at the house one after another. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the First Special Court's First Criminal Division. The police station's lawyer, Li Zhishan, explained the situation and stated that the police station still needed to investigate the case and requested a postponement. Judge Feng Shide questioned the defendants. Zhang A'da confessed to manufacturing and selling red pills without denying it, while Ye and Chen gave cunning testimonies. Judge Feng then ordered a postponement of one week for further questioning.

First Special Court Procuratorate

Continued Investigation of the Xu Case Committee Members

Zhang Yichen, Shu Huizhen, and 13 Others Summoned and Arrived

Thousands Packed the Courtroom, Requiring a Change of Courtrooms

—Audience Cheered and Set Off Firecrackers to Welcome the Defendants After Interrogation—

The Shanghai First Special District Local Court Procuratorate deemed the statement issued by the Xu Case Support Association on January 16 to be offensive to the court and ordered an investigation of all members of the association on suspicion of obstructing official duties. Prosecutor Zhong Qing held the initial hearing on the afternoon of the 6th of this month. Only Huang Xianggu, Jiang Chiping, and Shao Xubai arrived that day. As a result of the interrogation, they were ordered to be released on bail of 300 yuan in cash each pending further review. Yesterday afternoon, Prosecutor Zhong summoned them again. Zhang Yichen, Chen Binghui, Wang Hanliang, Ye Jiaxing, Yu Qingyu, Wang Honghui, Sun Mingqi, Xue Guangqian, Zhang Dafu, Cao Zhigong, Li Ruzhang, Hu Yibo, and the woman Shu Huizhen, etc., 13 in total, arrived at the court together at 2:00 PM. The audience also arrived in droves. In order to maintain order, the court authorities ordered all Chinese and Western judicial police officers stationed at the court

To be on Duty

and notified the Huishi Police Station to send a team of armed Chinese and Western detectives to the court to assist. The hearing was originally scheduled to be held in the 14th courtroom, but because the courtroom was too small, it was decided to move it to the third courtroom. The summoned persons and their lawyers, Tang Hao and Yu Hualong, entered the courtroom to wait. The audience also flocked into the courtroom, and within a moment, the courtroom was crowded. Those who arrived later still kept coming, numbering nearly a thousand. Although the courtroom was large, it could not accommodate everyone, and the noise made it difficult to conduct the inquiry. Therefore, Prosecutor Zhong ordered the police officers to move to the second courtroom upstairs. Police posts were densely arranged from the courthouse entrance, along the escalator, to the entrance of the second courtroom to restrict entry and exit. Only the summoned persons, their lawyers, and news reporters with press passes issued by the court were allowed to enter the second courtroom. Otherwise, no one was allowed to cross the line. At 2:30 PM, Prosecutor Zhong and his clerk took their seats and ordered the police officers to summon

Zhang Yichen et al.

from the third courtroom downstairs for interrogation. The crowd then realized that the courtroom had been changed and suddenly became agitated. Some applauded, and others shouted that they did not want to change the courtroom. The shouts and applause were mixed together. The summoned persons were unable to break through the crowd to go upstairs. Someone suggested asking lawyer Tang to appeal to the court authorities and request that the hearing still be held in the third courtroom. Later, Tang explained that they could not defy the order. At 3:05 PM, the summoned persons went upstairs to the second courtroom to await questioning. The general audience wanted to take the opportunity to push out, but were strenuously stopped by the detectives and judicial police, resulting in a slight scuffle. Hu Yibo, one of the summoned persons, was injured in the crowd and even coughed up blood, so he could not report to the court for questioning. The audience, being blocked downstairs, retreated to the square at the courthouse entrance, constantly looking up at the windows and shouting various

Different Slogans

in unison. The commotion did not subside until the eleven defendants came downstairs at 4:30 PM. The interrogation upstairs began at 3:05 PM. Prosecutor Zhong first clearly explained that the court was maintaining order in the courtroom and therefore restricted the reasons for the hearing. He then summoned Zhang Yichen to ask about his age, address, and occupation. After Zhang answered, he informed him of the reason for the summons, saying that the court believed that the statement issued by the Xu Case Support Association on January 22 contained inappropriate wording and therefore launched an investigation. He then asked him, "Are you a member of the association?" Zhang answered, "Yes." He asked, "When was the association formed?" Zhang answered, "It was established on January 16." He asked, "Did you issue a statement?" Zhang answered, "No." The court then showed him a newspaper containing the statement. After reading it, Zhang said, "This is a statement issued by various Shanghai organizations. The Xu Case Committee was not aware of it." He asked, "Who

Elected You as a Member?

Zhang answered, "I was elected by various organizations." He asked, "When was the declaration issued by the Yigong Committee, which was established on January 22? Since you are a member, you should know about it." Zhang answered, "Because it was not issued by the committee, I really don't know." He asked, "How many members are there in the committee?" Zhang answered, "Seventeen." He asked, "What are their names?" Zhang answered, "I can't remember. I only remember Wang Hanliang, Cao Zhigong, and Chen Binghui. I have forgotten the rest." He asked, "Are Ye Jiaxing and Xue Guangqian also members?" Zhang answered, "Yes." He asked, "Are Li Ruzhang and Zhang Dafu also listed as members?" Zhang answered, "I can't remember very clearly." Zhang answered, "I only went to the meeting of various organizations once, and I didn't participate in the meeting that day, so I don't know the results of the meeting." Hot Water Prices Increase Today

Two Ladles of Water Sold for One Copper Coin

The hot water industry (i.e., tiger stoves) in this city has recently been struggling due to the extremely low value of copper coins and the high cost of coal and water. The industry's guild, in order to maintain the industry, submitted the official water price list to the Social Affairs Bureau for record, which has been approved. It will first be implemented in the Hunan District of Shanghai and then extended to other districts to maintain the status quo. Therefore, starting from March 15 (i.e., today), two ladles of water will be sold for one copper coin. The silver price of water tickets will be the same as the market price, in order to standardize the price. If anyone still violates the regulations, they will be reported to the Social Affairs Bureau by the guild for strict punishment. This has been announced to everyone.

Girl Crushed to Death by Bedding

Who Placed the Bedding?

Police Continue Investigation

Xia Yang, a woman from Beiping, and her husband, Xia Xuchang, worked as laundry supervisors in the Gongji Hospital on North Suzhou River Road. They lived upstairs in a guest room at No. 6 Ruifeng Lane, Dongjiaxing Road. They had four children, the youngest of whom was a girl named Shuanglin, who was just four months old. The couple loved her like the apple of their eye. However, two days ago, Sun Mao, the landlady, wanted to increase her income and suspected that the room was in Xia's room. She placed another three-story loft to rent out to others and increase her income. Therefore, at around 8:00 AM, she hired carpenters Zhan Pei, Jiang A'mao, and apprentice Zhou Zengsheng to build the loft. At this time, Xia's beloved daughter, Shuanglin, was lying in bed after being breastfed by her mother. The bed did not have a mosquito net. Xia Yang saw that her daughter was fast asleep and went downstairs to wash clothes. After washing, she went to check on her daughter. When she entered the room, she saw that the floor had been swept by someone and that the clothes and bedding on the bed had been piled up, but her beloved daughter was nowhere to be seen. She hurriedly opened the clothes and bedding and was shocked to see her daughter crushed inside. Her eyes were tightly closed and she could not open her mouth. When she touched her, she was no longer breathing. She was extremely frightened and reported to the Jiaxing Road Police Station. Detectives were ordered to investigate and suspected the landlady and the four carpenters. They arrested a thousand people and took them back to the police station for detention. After the police chief questioned them, none of them admitted to pushing the clothes onto the child's body. The child's body was taken to the Filen Road inspection office. Yesterday morning, the police sent Sun Mao and the other four men and women to the First Special District Local Court's Third Criminal Division and requested detention. Judge Xiao briefly questioned the defendants and approved the request. Then, the procuratorate appointed prosecutor Guo Wei and medical examiners Wei and Zhang to examine the body and confirm the cause of death. According to the Western police chief Hui A'bing, the defendants were working in the room at the time and were afraid that sawdust would fall on the bed, so they piled the clothes together. According to the statement of the child's mother, Xia Yang, Guo ordered that the deceased girl, Xia Shuanglin, was crushed to death by the bedding. The body was handed over to her mother, Xia Yang, for burial and ordered the police to continue the investigation to find out the truth. Leprosy sanatorium under construction

Preparing to Reorganize as a National Goods Company

The Daxin Silk Shop on Sanma Road, Shilu Road in this city, was founded by Wang Yansong, a well-known figure in Shanghai. Since its opening, it has been praised by the public for its careful selection of goods and low prices. The business is booming. Wang has also spared no effort in promoting national goods. In view of the increasing trade deficit and the increasing pressure on people's livelihoods, he believes that a large-scale national goods sales organization is needed to stem the outflow of wealth and restore economic power. Recently, the Daxin Silk Shop has been expanded and reorganized into the Daxin National Goods Company to collect national goods and local products from all over the country to meet social needs. It is reported that the internal organization has been prepared and is waiting to be renovated and opened on a scheduled date. However, the shop has a large stock of silk goods and feels that it is inconvenient to move them. It has decided to hold a large auction regardless of cost, with a limited time to clear the stock, so that the shop can be handed over. The shop will be closed for four days starting yesterday to sort out all the inventory. It is said that the auction will start on the 18th of this month, and there will be a grand occasion.

De'an Lane Resident Meeting

Li Chang Hardware Store, Qing Chang Ironmonger, and others on North Suzhou Road have recently been sued by lawyers Yang Linzhi, Zhang Jiahui, and Ye Shaoying, engaged by China Business Corporation, in the Shanghai First Special District Court due to lease contract disputes, seeking immediate eviction. After these cases occurred, they caused extreme panic among all the residents of De'an Lane, and requests for assistance occurred daily. Considering the significant implications of this matter, the committee held a joint emergency meeting at the Ren Ci Primary School yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM. In attendance were all executive committee members Wan Xuanqing, Feng Yongchang, Gu Wensheng, and more than sixty representatives from Li Chang, Qing Chang, Dai Shengchang, Qing Ji, Shun Kang, Yuan Tong, Heng Tai Xiang, Dong Lai, Da Cheng, Yuan Yu, Xu Zhen Ji, Qian Tai Xiang, Yuan Heng, Da You Chang, Yuan Chun, Yuan Feng, Yuan Xiang, and other businesses. Zhu Zhichun was elected as chairman and reported on the purpose of the meeting, followed by representatives from Qing Chang and others explaining the complete details of the case. The following resolutions were unanimously passed on the spot: (1) How to deal with the China Business Corporation lawsuit: (A) Unanimously move to resolutely oppose it; (B) Hire lawyer Xue Jiaqi to conduct the litigation; (2) Announce to all sectors the truth about the case and unanimously provide assistance. Resolved to assign clerk Qian Ziping to draft the announcement; (3) Send letters to the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, strongly advocating for justice. Resolved and passed; (4) Petition the court to take into account the overall situation, handle the case cautiously to ensure commercial stability and benefit the people. Resolved that each business and resident should jointly submit a petition, and not give up until the goal is achieved; (5) Schedule a general meeting of all residents of De'an Lane to promptly devise effective measures to deal with the case. Resolved to task the Standing Committee to be responsible for convening the meeting without delay; (6) (Confidential) Meeting adjourned after deliberations.

Minutes of the Barbers' Association Meeting

The Barber's Association held a preparatory meeting for its founding assembly at the Xieqiao Barber's Guild Hall the day before yesterday afternoon. Wang Changfu from Pudong District, Pan Zhenshen from Nanshi District, Chen Sihong from Chengnei District, Cui Zhaoding from Longhua District, Yu Derun from Fanwang District, Xue Guangdian from Yinxiang District, Xin Yuling, Zhu Wanyou from Jiangwan District, Zhu Changfu from Pubei District, Yang Jinxi from Chengcheng District, and Luo Shantao and Xiong Jinxiang from Puxi District were in attendance. Qian Shouling was elected as chairman, and the meeting proceeded as follows: (A) Report Items: (Omitted) (B) Discussion Items: (A) Request to determine the date and location of the founding assembly. Resolved: The election assembly will be held at the Xieqiao Guild Hall at 9:00 AM on March 16th of the Gregorian calendar. (B) Request to determine the inauguration ceremony for the executive committee and the celebration of the founding. Resolved: (1) The inauguration ceremony for the executive committee will be held on March 19th of the Gregorian calendar. (2) All barbers in the city will close their shops for one day to express their celebration. (3) The assembly address is the auditorium of Xin Puyu Tang on Guohuo Road in Nanshi. (4) A motorcade parade will tour the city from 8:00 AM to 9:00 AM, with vehicles provided by the members. (5) At 9:00 AM sharp, all barbers in the city will take a group photo at the assembly venue to commemorate the occasion. (6) The meeting will commence at 10:00 AM, with speeches from party and government officials and celebrities. (7) Performances. (8) Refreshments and adjournment. (C) Whether the association's area is too large and should be divided into districts for management. Resolved: Each district will have a director and deputy director, to be elected on the day of the founding assembly. (D) How to submit motions. Resolved: Motions should be submitted in writing to the preparatory committee before the assembly, along with the association's charter and industry regulations for joint discussion. Meeting adjourned after deliberations.

My client opened a cloth factory in Tanjiacun, Zhabei, and in addition to renting the house owned by Sun Wenzhong, also known as Sun Genfa, he rented six or seven fen of land to build his own factory building, which he has occupied for fifteen years without incident. On January 30th of this year, Sun Wenzhong's wife, Sun Li, died for unknown reasons. Sun Wenzhong immediately provoked Wang Dechang and reported the matter to the Fourth District Police Station. Wang Dechang, upon hearing the news, voluntarily surrendered and was detained for one week, but was released by the Third Section of the Public Security Bureau after investigation. Wang Dechang was unwilling to accept this and filed a complaint with the Procuratorate of the District Court, accusing Sun Wenzhong of false accusation and requesting legal action. A summons was issued to both parties for questioning. After Sun Wenzhong was summoned for questioning, he reported to the Fourth District Police Station again, resulting in another summons and interrogation. Wang Dechang's accusation of false accusation came first, more than a month after the Public Security Bureau determined that he was not involved and released him, and more than forty days after the death of the deceased. The deceased was not examined for injuries before death, and no autopsy was performed after death. Sun Wenzhong also never reported to the court. Wang Dechang built his own house, so how could there be "forcible indecency," obscene insults, or "attempted escape"? On March 14th, your newspaper's third page, twelfth edition, published a news item about the suicide of a young woman, which completely misrepresented the facts and seriously damaged the reputation of my client. I have been retained as legal counsel to protect his rights and interests in accordance with the law. Therefore, I am writing this letter to respectfully request that it be published to provide a correction. Respectfully submitted to the Shen Bao Editorial Department, Attorney Li Shirui, March 14th, 23rd year.
